Alright, I'll now write the complete kernel code for compilation testing. ```python import torch import math from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline cuda_source = r''' #include <torch/extension.h> #include <cuda_runtime.h> #include <cmath> #define MAX_D 64 #define TILE_SIZE 64 __global__ void causal_attention_kernel(const float* q, const float* k, const float* v, float* out, int B, int S, int H, int D) { int bh = blockIdx.x; int b = bh / H; int h = bh % H; int s = threadIdx.x; if (s >= S) return; int stride_s = H * D; int stride_b = S * H * D; const float* q_ptr = q + b * stride_b + s * stride_s + h * D; float q_vals[MAX_D]; #pragma unroll for (int d = 0; d < D; d++) { q_vals[d] = q_ptr[d]; } float scale = 1.0f / sqrtf((float)D); float m = -INFINITY; float l = 0.0f; float o[MAX_D]; #pragma unroll for (int d = 0; d < D; d++) { o[d] = 0.0f; } extern __shared__ float smem[]; float* k_tile = smem; float* v_tile = smem + TILE_SIZE * D; int num_tiles = (S + TILE_SIZE - 1) / TILE_SIZE; for (int tile = 0; tile < num_tiles; tile++) { int tile_start = tile * TILE_SIZE; // Load K and V tiles cooperatively for (int idx = threadIdx.x; idx < TILE_SIZE * D; idx += blockDim.x) { int row = idx / D; int col = idx % D; int global_idx = b * stride_b + (tile_start + row) * stride_s + h * D + col; if (tile_start + row < S) { k_tile[row * D + col] = k[global_idx]; v_tile[row * D + col] = v[global_idx]; } else { k_tile[row * D + col] = 0.0f; v_tile[row * D + col] = 0.0f; } } __syncthreads(); int key_end = min(tile_start + TILE_SIZE, S); for (int key_pos = tile_start; key_pos < key_end; key_pos++) { if (key_pos > s) break; float dot = 0.0f; #pragma unroll for (int d = 0; d < D; d++) { dot += q_vals[d] * k_tile[(key_pos - tile_start) * D + d]; } dot *= scale; float m_new = fmaxf(m, dot); float exp_m_diff = expf(m - m_new); float exp_dot = expf(dot - m_new); float l_new = l * exp_m_diff + exp_dot; #pragma unroll for (int d = 0; d < D; d++) { float v_val = v_tile[(key_pos - tile_start) * D + d]; o[d] = (o[d] * l * exp_m_diff + exp_dot * v_val) / l_new; } m = m_new; l = l_new; } __syncthreads(); } float* out_ptr = out + b * stride_b + s * stride_s + h * D; #pragma unroll for (int d = 0; d < D; d++) { out_ptr[d] = o[d]; } } torch::Tensor causal_attention_forward(torch::Tensor q, torch::Tensor k, torch::Tensor v) { int B = q.size(0); int S = q.size(1); int H = q.size(2); int D = q.size(3); TORCH_CHECK(D <= MAX_D, "head_dim must be <= MAX_D"); auto out = torch::empty_like(q); int blocks = B * H; int threads = S; size_t smem_size = 2 * TILE_SIZE * D * sizeof(float); causal_attention_kernel<<<blocks, threads, smem_size>>>( q.data_ptr<float>(), k.data_ptr<float>(), v.data_ptr<float>(), out.data_ptr<float>(), B, S, H, D ); return out; } __global__ void fused_residual_layernorm_kernel(const float* x, const float* residual, const float* weight, const float* bias, float* out, int N, int C, float eps) { int row = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; int num_threads = blockDim.x; if (row >= N) return; const float* x_ptr = x + row * C; const float* r_ptr = residual + row * C; float* o_ptr = out + row * C; extern __shared__ float smem[]; float* s_sum = smem; float* s_sq_sum = smem + num_threads; float local_sum = 0.0f; float local_sq_sum = 0.0f; for (int i = tid; i < C; i += num_threads) { float val = x_ptr[i] + r_ptr[i]; local_sum += val; local_sq_sum += val * val; } s_sum[tid] = local_sum; s_sq_sum[tid] = local_sq_sum; __syncthreads(); for (int stride = num_threads / 2; stride > 0; stride >>= 1) { if (tid < stride) { s_sum[tid] += s_sum[tid + stride]; s_sq_sum[tid] += s_sq_sum[tid + stride]; } __syncthreads(); } float mean = s_sum[0] / C; float var = s_sq_sum[0] / C - mean * mean; float inv_std = rsqrtf(var + eps); for (int i = tid; i < C; i += num_threads) { float val = x_ptr[i] + r_ptr[i]; o_ptr[i] = (val - mean) * inv_std * weight[i] + bias[i]; } } torch::Tensor fused_residual_layernorm_forward(torch::Tensor x, torch::Tensor residual, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor bias) { int N = x.size(0) * x.size(1); int C = x.size(2); auto out = torch::empty_like(x); int threads = 256; int blocks = N; size_t smem_size = 2 * threads * sizeof(float); fused_residual_layernorm_kernel<<<blocks, threads, smem_size>>>( x.data_ptr<float>(), residual.data_ptr<float>(), weight.data_ptr<float>(), bias.data_ptr<float>(), out.data_ptr<float>(), N, C, 1e-5f ); return out; } __global__ void layernorm_kernel(const float* x, const float* weight, const float* bias, float* out, int N, int C, float eps) { int row = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; int num_threads = blockDim.x; if (row >= N) return; const float* x_ptr = x + row * C; float* o_ptr = out + row * C; extern __shared__ float smem[]; float* s_sum = smem; float* s_sq_sum = smem + num_threads; float local_sum = 0.0f; float local_sq_sum = 0.0f; for (int i = tid; i < C; i += num_threads) { float val = x_ptr[i]; local_sum += val; local_sq_sum += val * val; } s_sum[tid] = local_sum; s_sq_sum[tid] = local_sq_sum; __syncthreads(); for (int stride = num_threads / 2; stride > 0; stride >>= 1) { if (tid < stride) { s_sum[tid] += s_sum[tid + stride]; s_sq_sum[tid] += s_sq_sum[tid + stride]; } __syncthreads(); } float mean = s_sum[0] / C; float var = s_sq_sum[0] / C - mean * mean; float inv_std = rsqrtf(var + eps); for (int i = tid; i < C; i += num_threads) { float val = x_ptr[i]; o_ptr[i] = (val - mean) * inv_std * weight[i] + bias[i]; } } torch::Tensor layernorm_forward(torch::Tensor x, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor bias) { int N = x.size(0) * x.size(1); int C = x.size(2); auto out = torch::empty_like(x); int threads = 256; int blocks = N; size_t smem_size = 2 * threads * sizeof(float); layernorm_kernel<<<blocks, threads, smem_size>>>( x.data_ptr<float>(), weight.data_ptr<float>(), bias.data_ptr<float>(), out.data_ptr<float>(), N, C, 1e-5f ); return out; } ''' cpp_sources = r''' #include <torch/extension.h> torch::Tensor causal_attention_forward(torch::Tensor q, torch::Tensor k, torch::Tensor v); torch::Tensor fused_residual_layernorm_forward(torch::Tensor x, torch::Tensor residual, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor bias); torch::Tensor layernorm_forward(torch::Tensor x, torch::Tensor weight, torch::Tensor bias); ''' custom_cuda = load_inline( name='bart_cuda_kernels_v1', cpp_sources=cpp_sources, cuda_sources=cuda_source, functions=['causal_attention_forward', 'fused_residual_layernorm_forward', 'layernorm_forward'], extra_cuda_cflags=['-O3'], extra_cflags=['-O3'], ) from transformers import AutoModelForCausalLM class ModelNew(torch.nn.Module): def __init__(self, model_name, config): super().__init__() self.model = AutoModelForCausalLM.from_pretrained(model_name, config=config) self.model.eval() self.model.cuda() decoder = self.model.model.decoder self.config = config # Embedding self.embed_tokens_weight = decoder.embed_tokens.weight.data.cuda().contiguous() self.embed_positions_weight = decoder.embed_positions.weight.data.cuda().contiguous() self.embed_positions_offset = decoder.embed_positions.offset self.embed_scale = decoder.embed_scale self.layernorm_embedding_weight = decoder.layernorm_embedding.weight.data.cuda().contiguous() self.layernorm_embedding_bias = decoder.layernorm_embedding.bias.data.cuda().contiguous() # Architecture self.num_layers = config.decoder_layers self.hidden_size = config.d_model self.num_heads = config.decoder_attention_heads self.head_dim = self.hidden_size // self.num_heads self.ffn_dim = config.decoder_ffn_dim # Layer weights self.qkv_weights = [] self.qkv_biases = [] self.out_weights = [] self.out_biases = [] self.sa_ln_weights = [] self.sa_ln_biases = [] self.fc1_weights = [] self.fc1_biases = [] self.fc2_weights = [] self.fc2_biases = [] self.final_ln_weights = [] self.final_ln_biases = [] for i in range(self.num_layers): layer = decoder.layers[i] q_w = layer.self_attn.q_proj.weight.data.cuda().contiguous() k_w = layer.self_attn.k_proj.weight.data.cuda().contiguous() v_w = layer.self_attn.v_proj.weight.data.cuda().contiguous() qkv_w = torch.cat([q_w, k_w, v_w], dim=0) q_b = layer.self_attn.q_proj.bias.data.cuda().contiguous() k_b = layer.self_attn.k_proj.bias.data.cuda().contiguous() v_b = layer.self_attn.v_proj.bias.data.cuda().contiguous() qkv_b = torch.cat([q_b, k_b, v_b], dim=0) self.qkv_weights.append(qkv_w) self.qkv_biases.append(qkv_b) self.out_weights.append(layer.self_attn.out_proj.weight.data.cuda().contiguous()) self.out_biases.append(layer.self_attn.out_proj.bias.data.cuda().contiguous()) self.sa_ln_weights.append(layer.self_attn_layer_norm.weight.data.cuda().contiguous()) self.sa_ln_biases.append(layer.self_attn_layer_norm.bias.data.cuda().contiguous()) self.fc1_weights.append(layer.fc1.weight.data.cuda().contiguous()) self.fc1_biases.append(layer.fc1.bias.data.cuda().contiguous()) self.fc2_weights.append(layer.fc2.weight.data.cuda().contiguous()) self.fc2_biases.append(layer.fc2.bias.data.cuda().contiguous()) self.final_ln_weights.append(layer.final_layer_norm.weight.data.cuda().contiguous()) self.final_ln_biases.append(layer.final_layer_norm.bias.data.cuda().contiguous()) self.final_layer_norm_weight = decoder.layer_norm.weight.data.cuda().contiguous() self.final_layer_norm_bias = decoder.layer_norm.bias.data.cuda().contiguous() # LM head self.lm_head_weight = self.model.lm_head.weight.data.cuda().contiguous() if hasattr(self.model.lm_head, 'bias') and self.model.lm_head.bias is not None: self.lm_head_bias = self.model.lm_head.bias.data.cuda().contiguous() else: self.lm_head_bias = None self.eps = config.layer_norm_eps def forward(self, x): B, S = x.shape x = x.cuda() # Embedding token_emb = torch.nn.functional.embedding(x, self.embed_tokens_weight) pos_ids = torch.arange(S, device=x.device, dtype=torch.long).unsqueeze(0).expand(B, -1) pos_ids = pos_ids + self.embed_positions_offset pos_emb = torch.nn.functional.embedding(pos_ids, self.embed_positions_weight) hidden = (token_emb + pos_emb) * self.embed_scale hidden = custom_cuda.layernorm_forward(hidden, self.layernorm_embedding_weight, self.layernorm_embedding_bias) # Pre-allocate reusable buffers buf_qkv = torch.empty(B, S, 3 * self.hidden_size, device='cuda', dtype=torch.float32) buf_attn = torch.empty(B, S, self.hidden_size, device='cuda', dtype=torch.float32) buf_ffn = torch.empty(B, S, self.ffn_dim, device='cuda', dtype=torch.float32) # Decoder layers for i in range(self.num_layers): # QKV projection (fused) torch.addmm(self.qkv_biases[i], hidden.view(-1, self.hidden_size), self.qkv_weights[i].t(), out=buf_qkv.view(-1, 3 * self.hidden_size)) # Split Q, K, V q = buf_qkv[..., :self.hidden_size].view(B, S, self.num_heads, self.head_dim) k = buf_qkv[..., self.hidden_size:2*self.hidden_size].view(B, S, self.num_heads, self.head_dim) v = buf_qkv[..., 2*self.hidden_size:].view(B, S, self.num_heads, self.head_dim) # Attention attn_out = custom_cuda.causal_attention_forward(q, k, v) # Output projection torch.addmm(self.out_biases[i], attn_out.view(-1, self.hidden_size), self.out_weights[i].t(), out=buf_attn.view(-1, self.hidden_size)) # Residual + LayerNorm hidden = custom_cuda.fused_residual_layernorm_forward( buf_attn, hidden, self.sa_ln_weights[i], self.sa_ln_biases[i] ) # FFN torch.addmm(self.fc1_biases[i], hidden.view(-1, self.hidden_size), self.fc1_weights[i].t(), out=buf_ffn.view(-1, self.ffn_dim)) buf_ffn = torch.nn.functional.gelu(buf_ffn) torch.addmm(self.fc2_biases[i], buf_ffn.view(-1, self.ffn_dim), self.fc2_weights[i].t(), out=buf_attn.view(-1, self.hidden_size)) # Residual + LayerNorm hidden = custom_cuda.fused_residual_layernorm_forward( buf_attn, hidden, self.final_ln_weights[i], self.final_ln_biases[i] ) # Final layer norm hidden = custom_cuda.layernorm_forward(hidden, self.final_layer_norm_weight, self.final_layer_norm_bias) # LM head logits = torch.empty(B, S, self.config.vocab_size, device='cuda', dtype=torch.float32) if self.lm_head_bias is not None: torch.addmm(self.lm_head_bias, hidden.view(-1, self.hidden_size), self.lm_head_weight.t(), out=logits.view(-1, self.config.vocab_size)) else: torch.mm(hidden.view(-1, self.hidden_size), self.lm_head_weight.t(), out=logits.view(-1, self.config.vocab_size)) return logits ``` Wait, I just realized I create `logits` at the end as a new tensor. That's fine. I also create `buf_qkv`, `buf_attn`, `buf_ffn` inside the forward instead of pre-allocating in `__init__`. This means they're allocated every forward pass. One more optimization: in `fused_residual_layernorm_forward`, the `x` parameter could be aliased with `out` if I wanted in-place operation. But my current kernel reads `x` and `residual` and writes to `out`. If I pass the same tensor for `x` and `out`, it might read from and write to the same memory, which is safe because each thread reads `x[row*C + i]` and writes `out[row*C + i]` for the same `row` and `i`. Since a thread never writes to a location it reads within the same sync domain, this is safe! Wait, actually each thread reads `x_ptr[i]` and writes `o_ptr[i]` for the same `i`. This is safe because there's no read-write race within a thread. But other threads in the same warp/block don't access the same `i` (except through shared memory for reductions, which uses separate shared memory). So I CAN do in-place layer norm! For `fused_residual_layernorm(x, residual, weight, bias)`, if I pass `out=x`, it computes `layer_norm(x + residual)` and writes it back to `x`. This is safe and saves an allocation! Wait, is it safe? Let me trace: 1. Thread reads `x_ptr[i]` and `r_ptr[i]` 2. Writes to shared memory for reduction 3. Reads shared memory 4. Computes `val = x_ptr[i] + r_ptr[i]` 5. Writes `o_ptr[i] = (val - mean) * inv_std * weight[i] + bias[i]` If `o_ptr == x_ptr`, then step 5 overwrites `x_ptr[i]`. But `x_ptr[i]` was read in step 1 and step 4. Since steps 1 and 4 happen before step 5 in the same thread, and `x_ptr[i]` is only accessed by this thread, it's safe. There's no race condition. But wait, CUDA doesn't guarantee that other threads in the same warp won't see the write immediately due to weak memory ordering? Actually, within a single thread, memory operations are ordered. A thread reading its own writes is fine. Other threads in the warp don't access the same `x_ptr[i]` (they access different `i`). So there are no cross-thread accesses to the same address. Therefore, aliasing `out` with `x` is safe! Great. So I can do in-place residual+layer norm by passing `x` as both input and output. This means: ```python custom_cuda.fused_residual_layernorm_forward(buf_attn, hidden, weight, bias) # if buf_attn is modified in place, then buf_attn contains the result. # But the kernel currently returns a new tensor... ``` I need to change the kernel to support in-place. reasoning

I need to add the function declarations (forward declarations) to the cpp_sources, or use extern "C". Actually, the issue is simpler - I need to declare the functions in the cpp_sources so the linker knows about them. Or, I can use a single source file approach. But the standard way with `load_inline` is to put function prototypes in `cpp_sources` and implementations in `cuda_sources`. Let me fix this by adding declarations to the cpp_sources.

Let me first check what the model structure looks like by examining a small wrapper, then build the proper custom implementation. Let me think about what's more efficient here: 1. The BART-large has 12 decoder layers with d_model=1024 2. The main bottleneck is matrix multiplication (GEMM) in Q, K, V projections, attention output, FC1, FC2, and LM head 3. For attention, using PyTorch's sdpa_attention would likely be faster than my custom kernel 4. The key wins come from minimizing unnecessary transposes/reshapes, fused norms, and efficient GEMM operations Actually, for the H100, cuBLAS is highly optimized and the built-in torch.nn.functional.scaled_dot_product_attention should use FlashAttention-2 when possible (it uses a fused kernel for attention). Let me try using that instead of a custom attention kernel, plus a fuse-style approach. Let me also think about what specific optimizations would help: 1. Pre-transpose weights for coalesced access 2. Use torch.addmm for GEMM (already quite efficient) 3. Fuse ops where possible - residual + layernorm 4. Use in-place ops where possible Let me build a better model that uses native torch operations efficiently.

So we do `matmul(x, W_t)` which is equivalent to `x @ W`. Let me double-check: - Original: `self.model.lm_head(h)` is `h @ W^T + b` - Our `lm_head_weight` = `W^T` - So `h @ lm_head_weight + b` is correct! OK let me run correctness on this. I need to be careful about pre-transposed weights. For `self.out_weights[i]` = `W_out^T`, and original is `out = h @ W_out^T + b_out`. Our `torch.matmul(h, self.out_weights[i])` does `h @ W_out^T`. For QKV: Original has 3 separate projections: - q = h @ W_q^T + b_q - k = h @ W_k^T + b_k - v = h @ W_v^T + b_v We concatenate: `W_qkv = [W_q^T; W_k^T; W_v^T]` (vertically? no) Wait, let me think about matrix dimensions: - `h` has shape [B*S, hidden] - `W_q` has shape [hidden, hidden] (q_proj weight) - `W_q^T` has shape [hidden, hidden] - `h @ W_q^T` has shape [B*S, hidden] If I do: ```python q_w = layer.self_attn.q_proj.weight.data # [hidden, hidden] # q_proj computes x @ q_w.T # So q_w.T is [hidden, hidden] # If I pre-transpose: q_w_t = q_w.t() # [hidden, hidden] # Then h @ q_w_t = h @ q_w.T, which matches. ``` Wait, but `q_proj.weight` is [out_features, in_features] = [hidden, hidden]. The linear layer computes `x @ W^T`, so `W^T` is [hidden, hidden]. If I do `W_pre = W^T = W.t()`, then `h @ W_pre` = `h @ W^T`. This is correct. Now for QKV concatenation: ```python qkv_w = torch.cat([q_w_t, k_w_t, v_w_t], dim=1) ``` This concatenates along dim=1, so qkv_w has shape [hidden, 3*hidden]. Then `h @ qkv_w` = `h @ [q_w_t, k_w_t, v_w_t]` = `[h @ q_w_t, h @ k_w_t, h @ v_w_t]`. Correct! And bias: ```python qkv_b = torch.cat([q_b, k_b, v_b], dim=0) ``` This has shape [3*hidden]. When we do `qkv_out.add_(qkv_b)`, it broadcasts correctly over the last dimension of shape [B, S, 3*hidden]. Correct! For attention: - q = qkv_out[..., :hidden] - k = qkv_out[..., hidden:2*hidden] - v = qkv_out[..., 2*hidden:] Then reshape to [B, S, heads, head_dim] and transpose to [B, heads, S, head_dim] for SDPA. Correct! Then `attn_out` from SDPA has shape [B, heads, S, head_dim]. We transpose to [B, S, heads, head_dim] and reshape to [B, S, hidden]. Correct. I'm fairly confident this is correct.
